<div id="review_556247477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/556247477" />
    <a title="Aubrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey"><img alt="Aubrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472535045p2/4119460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aubrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aubrey" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey">Aubrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780394741048" href="/book/show/539477.Letters_to_a_Young_Poet">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aubrey by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/6431467-s-penkevich">s.penkevich</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556247477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16747278117778705213">Twelve years on and it will have been a ten <br/>by ten span of time since you left, Rilke.<br/>Left on high, left to below both word and<br/>hope, hope, most of all hope. Your heart you gave,<br/>and for that we love.<br/><br/>I'd like to rhyme in metered line along<br/>the likes of you, but too long ago your<br/>poetry graced my eyes. What lies left's a <br/>feeling fit for tears and joy alone, and<br/>somber light it is.<br/><br/>Your maudlin days do not astonish, for<br/>many a kindred of mine has suffered<br/>the same, and yet, goes on. I draw from each<br/>going </span>
  <span id="freeText16747278117778705213" style="display:none">Twelve years on and it will have been a ten <br />by ten span of time since you left, Rilke.<br />Left on high, left to below both word and<br />hope, hope, most of all hope. Your heart you gave,<br />and for that we love.<br /><br />I'd like to rhyme in metered line along<br />the likes of you, but too long ago your<br />poetry graced my eyes. What lies left's a <br />feeling fit for tears and joy alone, and<br />somber light it is.<br /><br />Your maudlin days do not astonish, for<br />many a kindred of mine has suffered<br />the same, and yet, goes on. I draw from each<br />going for my own, and yours I say is<br />of exquisite touch.<br /><br />Man to man you wrote back then, both letter<br />and the wider world of word, and as with<br />most I gritted firm for any and all<br />male strickenings of the female fact, of<br />grim necessity.<br /><br />But 'lo! You knew, and where you didn't, you<br />hoped, in a beauty of mournful bright. Of<br />early on you penned this plighted dream, and<br />did more in a quickening page than most<br />in their own lifetime.<br /><br />And more, and more, and more to come. Childhood<br />days, unhappy days, and yet every bloom<br />you would cherish and hold dear. Sin was not<br />a word allowed you said; what mattered was<br />life, and lived to love.<br /><br />In solitude and suspension flush, you<br />counseled attention paid to the soul of<br />self. Every part and every shuddering truth,<br />both internal and the real. Often faint,<br />often not enough.<br /><br />Fail better. The words came after you, and<br />with less heart, but you would most agree. There's<br />lovely things in life, you said, you wrote, you<br />sculpted deep in tears of crystalline. One<br />weeps in the knowing.<br /><br />But one would smile and cheer and cradle close<br />what you've left us dear. You felt, and saw fit<br />to refract as close to thought through form. To<br />all, to us, to me. I cannot return,<br />save for scripting here.<br /><br />Rainer Maria Rilke, you wrote; I<br />felt my heart would burst.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9343407652938059352">"Τα έργα τέχνης ζουν μέσα σε απέραντη μοναξιά, κι η κριτική είναι το χειρότερο μέσο για να τα ζυγώσεις."<br/><br/>Κάθε φορά που διαβάζω ένα βιβλίο σαν κι αυτό, συνειδητοποιώ πόσο μικροί και αδαής είμαστε σε σχέση με αυτό που ονομάζουμε ανθρώπινο πνεύμα.   <span id="freeText9343407652938059352" style="display:none">"Τα έργα τέχνης ζουν μέσα σε απέραντη μοναξιά, κι η κριτική είναι το χειρότερο μέσο για να τα ζυγώσεις."<br /><br />Κάθε φορά που διαβάζω ένα βιβλίο σαν κι αυτό, συνειδητοποιώ πόσο μικροί και αδαής είμαστε σε σχέση με αυτό που ονομάζουμε ανθρώπινο πνεύμα. Σε τι βάθη και σε τι κορυφές έχει φτάσει η σκέψη των μεγάλων δασκάλων μας και πόσα πράγματα θα μπορούσαμε να διδαχτούμε από αυτούς.<br />Ούτε οχτώ ζωές δεν θα έφταναν για να διαβάσουμε όλα τα βιβλία, να ακούσουμε όλες τις απόψεις και να κάνουμε όλες τις σκέψεις που θα μας επέτρεπαν, συνειδητοποιημένα και με πλήρη αντίληψη, να προχωρήσουμε κάτω από την επιφάνεια του μεγαλείου της ανθρώπινης ύπαρξης.<br /><br />Διαβάζοντας τα "Γράμματα σε ένα νέο ποιητή" του Ρίλκε, μπορούμε να γίνουμε λίγο σοφότεροι.</span>

<div id="review_1444868878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1444868878" />
    <a title="Perry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6354112-perry"><img alt="Perry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588528919p2/6354112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1444868878?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Perry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Perry" href="/user/show/6354112-perry">Perry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141192321" href="/book/show/13570789-letters-to-a-young-poet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6354112-perry?shelf=books-most-loved">books-most-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6354112-perry?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1444868878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15669910324447045080"><b>A Treasure Chest for Artists and Lovers of Art</b><br/><br/>I don't normally read a lot of poetry, but when considering this book a few years back, I'd read some of Rilke's poetry and the high praise I mention below. When I read this short book (80 pages) though, I had no idea what a true chest of treasures lies herein. I highlighted so much text and made so many notes, I noticed I left little text unscathed.<br/><br/>This book consists of ten letters written by Rainer Maria Rilke to a younger poet. It, and particularl</span>
  <span id="freeText15669910324447045080" style="display:none"><b>A Treasure Chest for Artists and Lovers of Art</b><br /><br />I don't normally read a lot of poetry, but when considering this book a few years back, I'd read some of Rilke's poetry and the high praise I mention below. When I read this short book (80 pages) though, I had no idea what a true chest of treasures lies herein. I highlighted so much text and made so many notes, I noticed I left little text unscathed.<br /><br />This book consists of ten letters written by Rainer Maria Rilke to a younger poet. It, and particularly this latest translation from German to English is well worth your time for its enlightenment on and encouragement of a love of life and art and of creativity. Somewhere I cannot now locate I read testimonials from some of the many great artists who have been deeply and positively affected by these letters over the past many decades.<br /><br /><i>To anyone reading this review who is considering creative writing</i>, I cannot stress enough the importance of reading this book, particularly as an invaluable counterbalance, in the name of Art and creativity above all else, to all the structural and technical writing tips you've likely been getting from all directions.<br /><br />Rainer Maria Rilke (1875-1926) was a Bohemian-Austrian poet, probably one of the most esteemed of all German-speaking poets and by many thought to be one of the greatest and most innovative in Western poetry. From the Poetry Foundation page on Rilke is this description: he "strove throughout his life to reconcile beauty and suffering, life and death, into one philosophy. ... For him Art was what mattered most in life." Poetry Foundation (internal cites omitted).<br /><br />The Guardian in its review of the new and best English translation of this book in May 2011 said, "And how could one not be glad to have lived long enough to read lines such as these: 'To love is also good, for love is hard. Love between one person and another: that is perhaps the hardest thing it is laid on us to do, the utmost, the ultimate trial and test, the work for which all other work is just preparation.'" <a href="https://goo.gl/lIQDuZ" rel="nofollow noopener">"Very good advice from on high"</a>, The Guardian, May 12, 2011 (quoting from this book).<br /><br />As a relative neophyte in appreciating poetry, I cannot do much more justice to the book than to quote you my favorite couple of passages: quotes: <blockquote> ...approach nature. Then try, like the first human being, to say what you see and experience and love and lose. ... flee general subjects and take refuge in those offered by your own day-to-day life; depict your sadnesses and desires, passing thoughts and faith in some kind of beauty—depict all this with intense, quiet, humble sincerity and make use of whatever you find about you to express yourself, the images from your dreams and the things in your memory. <br /><br />If your everyday life seems to lack material, do not blame it; blame yourself, tell yourself that you are not poet enough to summon up its riches, for there is no lack for him who creates and no poor, trivial place. And even if you were in a prison whose walls did not let any of the sounds of the world outside reach your senses—would you not have your childhood still, this marvelous, lavish source, this treasure-house of memories? Turn your attention towards that. Attempt to raise the sunken sensations of this distant past; your self will become the stronger for it, your loneliness will open up and become a twilit dwelling in which the noise other people make is only heard far off. <br /><br />And if from this turn inwards, from this submersion in your own world, there come verses, then it will not occur to you to ask anyone whether they are good verses. ... in them you will see your beloved natural possessions, a piece, and a voice, of your life. A work of art is good if it has arisen out of necessity. The verdict on it lies in this nature of its origin: there is no other. For this reason, my dear Sir, the only advice I have is this: to go into yourself and to examine the depths from which your life springs; at its source you will find the answer to the question of whether you have to write.<br /><br />****<br /><br />And if we only organize our life according to the principle which teaches us always to hold to what is difficult, then what now still appears most foreign will become our most intimate and most reliable experience. How can we forget those ancient myths found at the beginnings of all peoples? The myths about the dragons who at the last moment turn into princesses? Perhaps all the dragons in our lives are princesses, only waiting for the day when they will see us handsome and brave? Perhaps everything terrifying is deep down a helpless thing that needs our help.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15669910324447045080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3441903551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3441903551" />
    <a title="Annetius" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84919381-annetius"><img alt="Annetius" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602430568p2/84919381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3441903551?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annetius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annetius" href="/user/show/84919381-annetius">Annetius</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3441903551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5236259467238062245">Δε θέλω ψυχολόγο. Θέλω έναν Ράινερ Μαρία Ρίλκε να μου γράφει γράμματα.<br/><br/>Αν κανείς είναι ρομαντική κι ευαίσθητη ψυχή –μέσα του εννοώ και όχι κατά τα φαινόμενα- θα βρει μια πολύ ζεστή γωνιά στα γράμματα αυτά του Ράινε Μαρία Ρίλκε προς έναν νέο ποιητή ονόματι Κάπους και προς μια νέα γυναίκα, με άγνωστα στοιχεία. Αν δε είναι και από τη φύση του άνθρωπος που βρίσκει παρηγοριά στην τέχνη, όχι μόνο στη συγγραφή, θα αισθανθεί έντονα ότι τα γράμματα αυτά απευθύνονται στον ίδιο, ίσια μέσα στην καρδιά.<br/><br/>Ποια ε</span>
  <span id="freeText5236259467238062245" style="display:none">Δε θέλω ψυχολόγο. Θέλω έναν Ράινερ Μαρία Ρίλκε να μου γράφει γράμματα.<br /><br />Αν κανείς είναι ρομαντική κι ευαίσθητη ψυχή –μέσα του εννοώ και όχι κατά τα φαινόμενα- θα βρει μια πολύ ζεστή γωνιά στα γράμματα αυτά του Ράινε Μαρία Ρίλκε προς έναν νέο ποιητή ονόματι Κάπους και προς μια νέα γυναίκα, με άγνωστα στοιχεία. Αν δε είναι και από τη φύση του άνθρωπος που βρίσκει παρηγοριά στην τέχνη, όχι μόνο στη συγγραφή, θα αισθανθεί έντονα ότι τα γράμματα αυτά απευθύνονται στον ίδιο, ίσια μέσα στην καρδιά.<br /><br />Ποια είναι η συνθήκη για να ευδοκιμήσει η δημιουργία, η τέχνη, ο αληθινός εαυτός που κρύβεται κουλουριασμένος μέσα μας; Μα η μοναξιά φυσικά. Αλλά η μοναξιά σήμερα είναι κατά βάση κατακριτέα και μη επιθυμητή. Κι ενώ ζούμε σε εποχές βαθιάς μοναξιάς, το big bang των social media μας έχει καταπλακώσει και θεωρούμε ότι κοινωνικοποιούμαστε. Και δεν ξέρουμε τι να την κάνουμε τη μοναξιά ενώ θα μπορούσε να είναι η μαγιά για κάθε γέννηση, για κάθε κυοφορία και μητρότητα, από άνδρες και γυναίκες.<br /><br />Τις προάλλες, βρέθηκα στο πατρικό μου για να ποτίσω τα λουλούδια και ανακάλυψα ένα μεγάλο κουτί με δεκάδες γράμματα από το δημοτικό ακόμα, που αντάλλασσα με διάφορους ανθρώπους. Αφού έδωσα το credit στον εαυτό μου που έζησα την εποχή της αλληλογραφίας με αρκετά πλούσιο τρόπο, έπεσα σε ένα είδος μελαγχολίας που αυτή η εποχή έφυγε μια για πάντα και κυρίως γιατί η χάρη του γραπτού λόγου με μολύβι και χαρτί, με σημειωματάκια και σχεδιάκια πάνω στην αλληλογραφία, που εσωκλείει κάτι το πολύ πολύ προσωπικό, το πολύ ρομαντικό και το πολύ έντεχνο έχει εξαφανιστεί από τη ζωή μου εδώ και πολλά χρόνια. Και λυπήθηκα πραγματικά. Για κάτι τέτοιους λόγους θα ήθελα να ζω σε μια άλλη εποχή, για τη γοητεία της βραδύτητας, της υπομονής, της αναμονής που τσουρουφλίζει αλλά και εκπαιδεύει.  <br /><br />Αυτό ίσως θεωρηθεί μια παρένθεση, ωστόσο για μένα δεν είναι, ήταν μια από τις ουσιαστικές σκέψεις που μου προκάλεσε το μικρό αυτό βιβλίο.<br /><br />Χωρίς να έχω διαβάσει ποίηση του Ρίλκε, με αυτά τα γράμματα τρέφω συμπάθεια και τρυφερότητα απέναντί του. Γιατί και αυτός ο πεζός λόγος είναι καθόλα ποιητικός. Είναι δεκάδες οι φορές που κάνω σκέψεις βαθυστόχαστες και θα ήθελα αυτόματα με κάποιον τρόπο να καταγράφονται για να μη χαθούν, ωστόσο το γκρίζο σύννεφο της καθημερινότητας τσακίζει άτσαλα την κάθε δυνατότητα για καταγραφή τους. Συνειδητοποίησα πόσο αυτιστικά ζούμε μερικές φορές τις μέρες μας, αδυνατώντας να αφουγκραστούμε πού βρίσκεται η πραγματική πηγή μιας ευτυχίας που κατά βάθος όλοι επιθυμήσαμε αλλά μεταφέραμε στο περιθώριο της ζωής μας.<br /><br />Τα γράμματα αυτά ήταν ένα μεγάλο τσιρότο τρυφερότητας που καλύπτει επαρκώς όλη την περιοχή της καρδιάς. Υπάρχει πλούτος, υπάρχει διαύγεια, λεπτότητα συναισθημάτων, σφοδρότητα και μια ματιά προς τη γυναίκα από τις πιο ντελικάτες, τις πιο προς τα μέσα που έχω δει.<br /><br />Διαβάζοντας, φαντάστηκα τον ποιητή αποσυρμένο σε ένα κάστρο, μόνο του, να στοχάζεται και να δημιουργεί την τέχνη του και μπήκα σε ένα σύμπαν απόκοσμο, μακρινό, ζεστό και παγωμένο ταυτόχρονα, στοιχειωμένο και όμως γεμάτο με χιλιάδες άλλους κόσμους την ίδια στιγμή.<br /><br />"Κι όταν λέμε ότι ζούμε, δεν εννοούμε στην πραγματικότητα ότι κάθε τόσο σπάμε τα καλούπια στα οποία έχουμε μπει, για να απολαύσουμε με την καινούργια μας μορφή τη σχέση με τα άλλα πλάσματα που έλκονται μαγεμένα προς το ίδιο βασίλειο;"<br /><br />Ναι αγαπητέ ποιητή, έτσι θα πρέπει να είναι.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5236259467238062245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998842356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3028974287130425410"><b>Notes collected</b><br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/IsosVaE' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405604994i/10422896.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><a href='http://imgur.com/uQhMOM1' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405604994i/10422897._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/aUDqUOe' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439017902i/15782527.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Rilke, the lonely German-language poet, but not really a German, rather an exile for 10 years,...possessor of nothing, but his language, shows a young man how a "masterpiece of art" can be accomplished and last for long.</i><br/><br/><br/>Paris 1903.<br/><br/>It appears that Rilke had been approached by a poet asking for a critical view of his output. Yet, Rilke's standing was not critical, at all; he rather preferred a hearty (almost paternal) reply. So he advised the young poet to look inside,</span>
  <span id="freeText3028974287130425410" style="display:none"><b>Notes collected</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/IsosVaE" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405604994i/10422896.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><a href="http://imgur.com/uQhMOM1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405604994i/10422897._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/aUDqUOe" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439017902i/15782527.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Rilke, the lonely German-language poet, but not really a German, rather an exile for 10 years,...possessor of nothing, but his language, shows a young man how a "masterpiece of art" can be accomplished and last for long.</i><br><br><br>Paris 1903.<br><br>It appears that Rilke had been approached by a poet asking for a critical view of his output. Yet, Rilke's standing was not critical, at all; he rather preferred a hearty (almost paternal) reply. So he advised the young poet to look inside, instead of seeking others views and critics.<br><br>"Turn yourself inwards", was the sort of reply I am talking about; "investigate the cause for your writing"...seek its "roots" in your own heart. "Should I write"? ...if the young man gets a "yes", from his nightly meditations, then the next steps should be:<br><br>-don't approach general motives or love letters but,<br><br>-get close to Nature...focus on your own life,...your thoughts... your "faith in any form of beauty"<br><br>-and say it, with the uttermost "sincerity".<br><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/UzDCICr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405604994i/10422898.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>To the "creators" there's no poverty at all.<br><br> <i>Sounds simple,...<br><br>but it's not. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3028974287130425410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10782361164261256991">There is something very pious about the experience you have while reading this book. No, I am certainly not a theist. Not anymore. But if ever there were a Pantheon built for the bibliophiles, Rainer Maria Rilke’s “Letter To a Young Poet” shall invariably have a place in it. <br/><br/>Though this is just an account of Letters written by him to an aspiring poet, Rainer speaks to you in a language, which seems to be coming back to you, like a cherished memory once been forgotten. The Solitude he speaks abou</span>
  <span id="freeText10782361164261256991" style="display:none">There is something very pious about the experience you have while reading this book. No, I am certainly not a theist. Not anymore. But if ever there were a Pantheon built for the bibliophiles, Rainer Maria Rilke’s “Letter To a Young Poet” shall invariably have a place in it. <br /><br />Though this is just an account of Letters written by him to an aspiring poet, Rainer speaks to you in a language, which seems to be coming back to you, like a cherished memory once been forgotten. The Solitude he speaks about has already been there, but is rekindled when his chord strikes it to life, transcending a century and many countries in between. And what an effect it produces! Quietening you in your entirety and compelling you to believe once more. <br /><br /><i>I am sure I shall keep getting back to it...</i><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13334867285473704295">I could just paste here all the passages I highlighted while reading this last month during my breaks from writing--but that would mean pasting practically the entire book.<br/>Because it is that good.<br/>You don't have to be a writer to truly enjoy this heartwarming read. Through this correspondence revolving around the writing craft, Rilke gives us glimpses into his general worldview and way of life convictions. His insight and existential approach on themes like anxiety, solitude and empathy are deepl</span>
  <span id="freeText13334867285473704295" style="display:none">I could just paste here all the passages I highlighted while reading this last month during my breaks from writing--but that would mean pasting practically the entire book.<br />Because it is that good.<br />You don't have to be a writer to truly enjoy this heartwarming read. Through this correspondence revolving around the writing craft, Rilke gives us glimpses into his general worldview and way of life convictions. His insight and existential approach on themes like anxiety, solitude and empathy are deeply relatable in our very own day and age as well.<br />Icing on the cake: his feminist views, at least in this book, for which he undeniably deserves even more credit.<br />A must-read.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Perhaps you will discover that you are called to be an artist. Then take that destiny upon yourself, and bear it, its burden and its greatness, without ever asking what reward might come from outside. For the creator must be a world for himself and must find everything in himself."</b>
</i></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2913141540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16783769504768622710"><b>السخرية؛ لا تتركها تسيطر عليك، وبخاصة في اللحظات التي يغيب فيها الإبداع. أما في لحظات الإبداع فحاول أن تسغلها، بوصفها وسيلة إضافية لفهم الحياة. إذا استخدمتها بنقاء ستبقي نقية ولن يكون عليك أن تخجل منها. وإذا شعرت أنك ألفتها أكثر مما ينبغي، فاخش تلك الألفة المتزايدة وأدر دفتك صوب أمور عظيمة وجادة تبدو السخرية أمامها ضئيلة وعاجزة. ابحث عن أعماق الأشياء، فهناك لا يمكن أن تسقط السخرية أبدا. وعندما تقترب من حافة ذلك الأمر الكبير، اختبر في الوقت ذاته إذا كانت طريقة الفهم هذه تنبع كامنة من كيانك. لأنها</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16783769504768622710" style="display:none"><b>السخرية؛ لا تتركها تسيطر عليك، وبخاصة في اللحظات التي يغيب فيها الإبداع. أما في لحظات الإبداع فحاول أن تسغلها، بوصفها وسيلة إضافية لفهم الحياة. إذا استخدمتها بنقاء ستبقي نقية ولن يكون عليك أن تخجل منها. وإذا شعرت أنك ألفتها أكثر مما ينبغي، فاخش تلك الألفة المتزايدة وأدر دفتك صوب أمور عظيمة وجادة تبدو السخرية أمامها ضئيلة وعاجزة. ابحث عن أعماق الأشياء، فهناك لا يمكن أن تسقط السخرية أبدا. وعندما تقترب من حافة ذلك الأمر الكبير، اختبر في الوقت ذاته إذا كانت طريقة الفهم هذه تنبع كامنة من كيانك. لأنها تحت تأثير الأمور الجادة إما ستغيب عنك (إذا كانت شئيا عارضا)، وإما ستصبح (إذا كانت متأصلة فيك) أقوي، لتتحول إلي أداة جادة تندرج في سلسلة الوسائل التي عليك أن تصيغ بها فنك.<br /></b><br />من رسائل راينر ماريا ريلكه إلي صديقه الشاب</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115407803" />
    <a title="Evan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1248986-evan"><img alt="Evan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488574589p2/1248986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115407803?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan" href="/user/show/1248986-evan">Evan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780394741048" href="/book/show/539477.Letters_to_a_Young_Poet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=essay-critique-short-form-or-memoir">essay-critique-short-form-or-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=__in-my-collection">__in-my-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=my-faves">my-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=epistle-larry-approves">epistle-larry-approves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115407803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2247938774509673885"><br/>Sigh. Rilke answers nothing and answers everything.<br/><br/>He talks of our ancestors as being "murmuring blood." This book, containing the voice of his wisdom across the age, is blood that courses through us and speaks.<br/><br/>It offers comfort to me in the face of life's challenges, its unrequited longings. It helps me see the value of difficulties and the importance of patience.<br/><br/>I wish I'd read this many years ago. I think it would have given me guidance I needed, even if it didn't lead me away from mistakes. </span>
  <span id="freeText2247938774509673885" style="display:none"><br />Sigh. Rilke answers nothing and answers everything.<br /><br />He talks of our ancestors as being "murmuring blood." This book, containing the voice of his wisdom across the age, is blood that courses through us and speaks.<br /><br />It offers comfort to me in the face of life's challenges, its unrequited longings. It helps me see the value of difficulties and the importance of patience.<br /><br />I wish I'd read this many years ago. I think it would have given me guidance I needed, even if it didn't lead me away from mistakes. Rilke knows the mistakes are essential.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2247938774509673885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bqQCZb8SfHS/l70zkhsDBCuG8bTuE2Ln5acF3YTMIFpUgmu3BEy1HBi8CVJl7gnb/dkWfCCe7IC+2UNsSY/SwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

قيد الحياة الوقت الكافي فقط لرد الضربة على ظالميه» - «ألان فورست»\n\nبصراحة مُؤثِّرة ومُبهرة قلَّ <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14931559348959343110\" style=\"display:none\">•	«يستحق «فالادا» ثناءً عاليًا لكتابته عن الحياة بهذه الواقعية، وهذا الصدق، وهذا القرب» - «هرمان هسه»\n•	«يمكن اعتبار «فالادا» بطلًا، كاتبًا بطلًا بقي على قيد الحياة الوقت الكافي فقط لرد الضربة على ظالميه» - «ألان فورست»\n\nبصراحة مُؤثِّرة ومُبهرة قلَّ نظيرها في الأدب العالمي، يخبرنا «هانز فالادا» عن السلوك القهري لمدمن المورفين، إذ عرف من خبرته الخاصة نشوة لحظة التعاطي والكارثة التي تليها.\nتعود كتابة «تقرير موضوعي عن سعادة مدمن المورفين» إلى ثلاثينيات القرن العشرين، إلا أن النَّص لم يُنشر قبل نهاية التسعينيات.\nأما النَّص الثاني في هذه المجموعة، والذي كُتب في الفترة نفسها، «ثلاث سنوات لم أكن إنسانًا»، فيتناول تجربة السجن، وهو أيضًا مُستوحى من حياة المؤلف.\nينجح «فالادا»، على الرغم من أسلوبه الموضوعي الجاف الذي يندرج في تيار «الموضوعية الجديدة»، أو ربما بفضل هذا الأسلوب، في صياغة نصَّين آسرين، شيِّقين، وقويَّين في صدقهما، وسُخريتهما، وفرادتهما في تاريخ الأدب الحديث.\nنُقدِّم القصتين هنا كأول أعمال «فالادا» بالعربية، وقد ترجمهما عن الألمانية سمير جريس ببراعة غنية عن التوصيف.\n\n•	«كل شيء في حياتي ينتهي في كتاب» - «هانس فالادا»\n\n«هانس فالادا» (1893-1947)، واسمه الحقيقي «رودولف ديتسن»، من أشهر الكُتاب الألمان في القرن العشرين. بأسلوبه الموضوعي الجاف الذي يندرج في تيار «الموضوعية الجديدة» كتبَ عددًا من الروايات الاجتماعية الكبيرة التي حققت نجاحًا باهرًا، مثل رواية «ماذا بعد، أيها الرجل الصغير؟» (1932)، التي عالج فيها الانحدار الاجتماعي الذي شهده موظف بسيط خلال الأزمة الاقتصادية التي اجتاحت العالم في عشرينيات القرن الماضي. حققت هذه الرواية نجاحًا عالميًّا، تكرر في أعماله اللاحقة مثل «ذئب بين ذئاب» (1937) و«كلٌّ يموت من أجل نفسه فحسب» (1947).\nلم تفقد أعمال «فالادا» راهنيتها وأهميتها حتى اليوم، فما زالت تصدر في طبعات جديدة، وما زالت تُترجم وتُعاد ترجمتها إلى عديد من لغات العالم، كما تحول عدد كبير من أعماله إلى أفلام سينمائية وأعمال مسرحية.\nقضى «فالادا» فترات من حياته في مصحات العلاج من إدمان المورفين، كما وقع فريسة إدمان الخمر، ولذلك كان الإدمان موضوعًا مسيطِرًا على بعض أعماله التي صدرت بعد وفاته، مثل رواية «السكير» (كتبها عام 1944 وصدرت للمرة الأولى عام 1950) ومجموعة «تقرير موضوعي عن سعادة مدمن المورفين» التي صدرت لأول مرة عام 1997، ومنها اخترنا قصتَي هذا الكتاب، اللتين تترجمان إلى العربية للمرة الأولى.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14931559348959343110\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7906.Rainer_Maria_Rilke">About Rainer Maria Rilke</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12990838707881562698">Rainer Maria Rilke is considered one of the German language's greatest 20th century poets. <br/><br/>His haunting images tend to focus on the difficulty of communion with the ineffable in an age of disbelief, solitude, and profound anxiety — themes that tend to position him as a transitional figure between the traditional and the modernist poets.<br/><br/>He wrote in both verse and a highly lyrical prose. His two mos</span>
  <span id="freeText12990838707881562698" style="display:none">Rainer Maria Rilke is considered one of the German language's greatest 20th century poets. <br /><br />His haunting images tend to focus on the difficulty of communion with the ineffable in an age of disbelief, solitude, and profound anxiety — themes that tend to position him as a transitional figure between the traditional and the modernist poets.<br /><br />He wrote in both verse and a highly lyrical prose. His two most famous verse sequences are the <i>Sonnets to Orpheus</i> and the <i>Duino Elegies</i>; his two most famous prose works are the <i>Letters to a Young Poet</i> and the semi-autobiographical <i>The Notebooks of Malte Laurids Brigge</i>. <br /><br />He also wrote more than 400 poems in French, dedicated to his homeland of choice, the canton of Valais in Switzerland.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12990838707881562698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1208289-briefe-an-einen-jungen-dichter">Quotes from Letters to a Youn...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Perhaps all the dragons in our lives are princesses who are only waiting to see us act, just once, with beauty and courage. Perhaps everything that frightens us is, in its deepest essence, something helpless that wants our love.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/745-perhaps-all-the-dragons-in-our-lives-are-princesses-who">11094 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Therefore, dear Sir, love your solitude and try to sing out with the pain it causes you. For those who are near you are far away... and this shows that the space around you is beginning to grow vast.... be happy about your growth, in which of course you can't take anyone with you, and be gentle with those who stay behind; be confident and calm in front of them and don't torment them with your doubts and don't frighten them with your faith or joy, which they wouldn't be able to comprehend. Seek out some simple and true feeling of what you have in common with them, which doesn't necessarily have to alter when you yourself change again and again; when you see them, love life in a form that is not your own and be indulgent toward those who are growing old, who are afraid of the aloneness that you trust.... and don't expect any understanding; but believe in a love that is being stored up for you like an inheritance, and have faith that in this love there is a strength and a blessing so large that you can travel as far as you wish without having to step outside it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/140777-therefore-dear-sir-love-your-solitude-and-try-to-sing">2763 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
